## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Stress typically increases with strain through elastic and plastic regimes, while temperature generally reduces material strength through thermal softening.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * T) * epsilon (Hooke's law with thermal softening of elastic modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic flow)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with power hardening)
- Arrhenius thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power law for pre-strained materials)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (nonlinear elastic-plastic)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (exponential temperature dependence)
- Bilinear model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon * T (linear coupling of strain and temperature)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (sinh-type creep/flow law)
- Polynomial hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) * (c2 + c3 * T + c4 * T**2) (polynomial in both variables)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening factor (1 - T/T_melt) → multiplicative term (1 - c*T) or (c0 - c1*T) representing loss of strength at high temperature
- Strain hardening saturation → exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), indicating dislocation density saturation
- Arrhenius-type temperature dependence → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) reflecting thermally activated dislocation motion
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain and temperature effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), reflecting separability of hardening and thermal softening
- Concave-down stress-strain curves → power law epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or logarithmic log(1+c*epsilon), reflecting diminishing work hardening
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as ratio c0*T or shifted (T - c1) reflecting proximity to melting point
- Strain offset for yield → (epsilon + c0)**c1 or max(epsilon - c0, 0) representing elastic-to-plastic transition
- Inverse temperature dependence → terms like c0/T appearing in exponents, characteristic of Zener-Hollomon type thermally activated processes

None of the candidates seem to have both `T*log(epsilon+1)` AND `epsilon^c * exp(-c/T)` simultaneously.

**Candidate 36**: `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon + T*c2*log(c3*epsilon+1) + c4*log(c3*epsilon+1) + c5 + c6*epsilon^c7 + c8*epsilon/(c9*epsilon+1)`

The `epsilon/(c9*epsilon+1)` and remaining terms can't produce this.

After careful analysis, none of the candidates contain the critical structural element of `epsilon^c * exp(c/T)` combined with `T*log(epsilon+1)`.
